Romain Dillet
Senior Reporter


Romain Dillet is a Senior Writer at TechCrunch.
He has written over 2,500 articles on technology and tech startups and has established himself as an influential voice on the European tech scene. He has a deep background in startups, privacy, blockchain, security, fintech, mobile, social and media.
With eight years of experience at TechCrunch, he’s one of the familiar faces of the tech publication that obsessively covers Silicon Valley and the tech industry. In fact, his career started at TechCrunch when he was 21. Based in Paris, many people in the tech ecosystem consider him as the most knowledgeable tech journalist in town.
Romain likes to spot important startups before anyone else. He was the first person to cover N26, Revolut and DigitalOcean. He has written scoops on large acquisitions from Apple, Microsoft and Snap.
When he’s not writing, Romain is also a developer — he understands how the tech behind the tech works. He also has a deep historical knowledge of the computer industry for the past 50 years. He knows how to connect the dots between innovations and the effect on the fabric of our society.
Romain graduated from Emlyon Business School, a leading French business school specialized in entrepreneurship. He has helped several non-profit organizations, such as StartHer, an organization that promotes education and empowerment of women in technology, and Techfugees, an organization that empowers displaced people with technology.
Disclosure: Romain owns small amounts of various cryptocurrencies.

Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0 The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly grabs $166 million to help real estate investors reduce carbon emissions"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.deepki.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Deepki<\/a> has raised a $166 million Series C funding round (\u20ac150 million). The company is building a software-as-a-service platform for the real estate industry. It\u2019s a monitoring and analytics product that helps you take better decisions.<\/p>\n<p>Companies using Deepki can track and analyze ESG (Environmental, Social, and Governance) criteria, starting with carbon emissions generated by their real estate portfolio.<\/p>\n<p>You can\u2019t reduce what you can\u2019t measure. As real estate investors want to lower their environmental impact with new and existing projects, Deepki first lets you get a comprehensive overview of your carbon emission performance.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292319\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Deepki lets you collect and aggregate data, such as energy, water and waste. The company tries to automate this process as much as possible using APIs, web scraping or connections to SFTP servers.<\/p>\n<p>It can be a good starting point to see how you stack up compared to legal requirements across various geographies. You can also extract data and use it for certifications.<\/p>\n<p>But using a product like Deepki can be particularly useful to see trends over time. From Deepki\u2019s data management and monitoring platform, you can see how your electricity or water consumption changes over time.<\/p>\n<p>Big corporate clients with multiple commercial properties can add several locations to Deepki and compare them on the platform. This way, you can prioritize one building over another to implement energy savings plans. It\u2019ll improve your overall carbon trajectory.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The Series C round has been led by Highland Europe and One Peak Partners. Bpifrance\u2019s Large Venture fund and Revaia are also participating in the investment. Some existing investors are also putting more money on the table, such as Hi Inov and Statkraft Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe global real estate sector needs to act now if it is to halve its emissions by 2030 and meet the net zero target by 2050. This represents a huge market opportunity for Deepki. Today\u2019s new funding announcement means that Deepki can make a greater impact and support even more asset owners in taking on the climate change challenge, and we are pleased to have our new partners Highland Europe and One Peak, as well as Revaia and Bpifrance Large Venture on this journey,\u201d co-founder and CEO Vincent Bryant said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>As you can see, Deepki develops a highly specific SaaS platform for clients with very specific needs. That\u2019s why the company also has a consulting service to help Deepki\u2019s customers implement ESG strategies and action plans.<\/p>\n<p>The company currently has 150 employees across five European capital cities. Deepki currently monitors buildings in 38 different countries, which represent over 500 million square meters. Clients include AEW, Tikehau, Generali RE, DeA Capital, Allianz Real Estate, Warburg HIH, Azora Capital and Neinver.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup Deepki has raised a $166 million Series C funding round (\u20ac150 million). The company is building a software-as-a-service platform for the real estate industry. It\u2019s a monitoring and analytics product that helps you take better decisions. Companies using Deepki can track and analyze ESG (Environmental, Social, and Governance) criteria, starting with carbon emissions SaaS","slug":"vertical-saas","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576885804"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576885804"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2291619,"date":"2022-03-31T00:00:46","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T07:00:46","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2291619"},"modified":"2022-03-31T07:25:51","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T14:25:51","slug":"klarna-launches-new-klarna-kosma-division-for-its-open-banking-platform","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/klarna-launches-new-klarna-kosma-division-for-its-open-banking-platform\/","title":{"rendered":"Klarna launches new Klarna Kosma division for its open banking platform"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Visa surprised the European fintech industry last year when it <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/24\/visa-to-acquire-open-banking-platform-tink-for-more-than-2-billion\/\">announced<\/a> that it would acquire <a href=\"https:\/\/tink.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Tink<\/a> for \u20ac1.8 billion ($2.15 billion at the time of the deal). Klarna now wants to compete directly with Tink with a new business unit that has its own brand \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kosma.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Klarna Kosma<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Like Tink, Klarna offers an open banking application programming interface (API) with Klarna Kosma. Tink and Klarna are also both headquartered in Stockholm, Sweden. There are other open banking API companies, such as <a href=\"https:\/\/truelayer.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TrueLayer<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/plaid.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Plaid<\/a>. And it&#8217;s been a competitive space as Visa also tried to acquire Plaid but that deal <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/12\/visa-will-not-acquire-plaid-after-running-into-regulatory-wall\/\">fell through<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>With this new strategy, Klarna is essentially saying that it\u2019s open for business. If you\u2019re building a financial product and need to interact with bank accounts, you have one more option.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2291619\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Klarna Kosma is an API that other companies can integrate in their apps and services. These companies can leverage Klarna\u2019s API to access account statements, initiate payments, fetch banking information and refresh this data regularly.<\/p>\n<p>Klarna is better known for its &#8220;buy now, pay later&#8221; products. In some countries, Klarna lets customers connect to their bank account to give spending insights and establish a sort of credit score before letting customers buy something in multiple installments. With today\u2019s move, Klarna is opening up its in-house product to other customers.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWith Kosma we are opening up the power of our proprietary Open Banking platform and technology to banks, merchants and fintechs who share our dream of a world where consumers own their data and banks compete for customers by delivering value, not by locking in data,\u201d Klarna CTO Yaron Shaer said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>In Europe, banks and financial institutions all have to offer open banking interfaces due to the EU\u2019s Payment Services Directive PSD2. But there\u2019s no single standard. Open banking APIs do the heavy lifting for you.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Klarna said that it covers 15,000 banks across 24 countries. The API mostly focuses on European and American banks so far, but it plans to expand to other markets soon, such as Australia, Canada and New Zealand.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to Account Information Service (AIS), Klarna Kosma customers can also programmatically initiate payments with compatible banks. That has always been the long-term promise of open banking. If payment initiation takes off, it could replace card payments or e-wallets like PayPal. We\u2019re not there yet, but Klarna definitely wants to have a product ready if we get there.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Visa surprised the European fintech industry last year when it announced that it would acquire Tink for \u20ac1.8 billion ($2.15 billion at the time of the deal). Klarna now wants to compete directly with Tink with a new business unit that has its own brand \u2014 Klarna Kosma. Like Tink, Klarna offers an open banking adds limited Markdown support to Google Docs"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Google shared <a href=\"http:\/\/workspaceupdates.googleblog.com\/2022\/03\/compose-with-markdown-in-google-docs-on.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a blog post<\/a> with Google Workspace customers announcing some good news for all <a href=\"https:\/\/en.wikipedia.org\/wiki\/Markdown\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Markdown<\/a> fans out there. Google Docs can now automatically convert Markdown formatting to rich text.<\/p>\n<p>If you\u2019re not familiar with Markdown, this markup language has become very popular over the past few years if you want to write structured documents \u2014 and especially web content. For instance, popular note-taking tools like <a href=\"https:\/\/www.notion.so\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Notion<\/a> or <a href=\"https:\/\/bear.app\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bear<\/a> support Markdown. Content management systems like WordPress also let you <a href=\"https:\/\/wordpress.com\/support\/wordpress-editor\/blocks\/markdown-block\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">enable Markdown<\/a> as a way to write new posts.<\/p>\n<p>This new feature for Google Docs is off by default. You have to manually turn it on in the settings first. That\u2019s why I\u2019m writing this post. If you want to enable Markdown support, open a document in Google Docs, head over to the top of the screen, go to &#8220;Tools&#8221; then &#8220;Preferences&#8221; and enable &#8220;Automatically detect Markdown.&#8221; After that, you\u2019re good to go. If you can&#8217;t see the feature today, that&#8217;s normal, as the company is rolling out the new feature progressively over the coming days.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2291537\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Again, don\u2019t expect extensive Markdown support. Google Docs is still a rich text editor and this isn\u2019t going to magically change once you enable the Markdown feature.<\/p>\n<p>Instead, Google Docs will replace common Markdown formatting with rich text. For instance, you can create links with parentheses and brackets like <code>[this](https:\/\/techcrunch.com)<\/code>. You can italicize text by surrounding it with the <code>*<\/code> character.<\/p>\n<p>Google Docs supports different levels of headings, bold, italic, strikethrough and links. Numbered lists and unstructured lists still get automatically formatted like before.<\/p>\n<p>In other words, this new feature complements some keyboard shortcuts. It also makes it easier to copy Markdown content from one app to Google Docs, which can be particularly useful if you use a Markdown editor like <a href=\"https:\/\/ulysses.app\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ulysses<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>But\u2026 that doesn\u2019t work the other way. What\u2019s great about Markdown is that it\u2019s a plain text format that is compatible with multiple apps and services.<\/p>\n<p>For instance, Google Docs should let you natively export the current document as Markdown so that you can quickly copy and paste it anywhere Markdown is supported. I know, there is a plugin for that. But not all companies are comfortable with plugins.<\/p>\n<p>Hey Google, it\u2019s a nice first step, but you have to iterate and offer more Markdown features, please.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-2291545\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?w=660\" alt=\"\" width=\"660\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg 1118w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?resize=146,150 146w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?resize=291,300 291w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?resize=768,791 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?resize=660,680 660w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-30-at-6.51.04-PM.jpeg?resize=32,32 32w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 660px) 100vw, 660px\" \/><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Google shared a blog post with Google Workspace customers announcing some good news for all Markdown fans out there. Google Docs can now automatically convert Markdown formatting to rich text. If you\u2019re not familiar with Markdown, this markup language has become very popular over the past few years if you want to write structured documents with subpar soundbars, Devialet releases high-end soundbar"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Meet the Devialet Dione, a brand new speaker from high-end speaker manufacturer <a href=\"https:\/\/www.devialet.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Devialet<\/a>. With this new product, the company is entering a new market \u2014 home cinema sound systems. The Devialet Dione is an all-in-one soundbar compatible with Dolby Atmos 5.1.2 and it costs $2,400 (\u20ac2,190).<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are at the high end of the market but we have a product that is an all-in-one audio system,\u201d Devialet CEO Franck Lebouchard told me. What he means by that is that you shouldn\u2019t compare the Dione with an average soundbar.<\/p>\n<p>For instance, if you\u2019re trying to find an equivalent device in Sonos\u2019 lineup, Lebouchard says you should compare Devialet\u2019s speaker with the Sonos Arc soundbar paired with two Sonos One speakers and a Sonos Sub. And that package currently costs more than $2,000 as well.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290202\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThe tech achievement is that we managed to put everything in a single device. It means that we had to make 17 speakers fit, which is unheard of,\u201d Lebouchard added.<\/p>\n<p>The company set up a testing room in its office in Paris and I could listen to the Devialet Dione with a large TV. We tried the speaker with the first few scenes of Mad Max: Fury Road. We also listened to some music.<\/p>\n<p>And, sure enough, the speaker sounds great. It produces some immersive sound and it feels like you\u2019re sitting in a movie theater rather than in front of a TV.<\/p>\n<p>This isn&#8217;t a full review. I\u2019m not an audio professional, so I don\u2019t know how the Devialet soundbar sounds when you compare it with the current top-of-the-line soundbars. I would recommend listening to the Devialet Dione in a store before buying it anyway.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIn a Sennheiser soundbar, you\u2019ll find 12 speakers. We put 17 speakers. It\u2019s not completely magical, but when you can fit five more speakers in it, you can hear it,\u201d Lebouchard said.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2290203\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2290203\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2290203\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=768,768 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=1536,1536 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/3D-open-Devialet-Dione_3.jpeg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2290203\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Devialet<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The device itself is a dense soundbar. It weighs 12kg and it is quite long \u2014 1.2 meters. You should think about getting a speaker like that if you already have a very large 55-inch TV.<\/p>\n<p>When it comes to design, it is a bit more discreet than previous Devialet speakers. The signature egg-shaped Devialet design has been replaced with a more traditional polygon with sharp edges and corners.<\/p>\n<p>The only thing that stands out is a tiny sphere at the center of the device. There\u2019s a speaker inside that sphere and it pivots. This way, if you want to fix the soundbar to the wall, you can rotate the sphere so that it\u2019s always facing you.<\/p>\n<p>Inside the device, there are 17 different speakers \u2014 nine full-range drivers and eight rectangle subwoofers. Those subwoofers have been designed to fit the specifications of a soundbar. Again, what makes the Devialet Dione stand apart is that you don\u2019t need a separate subwoofer (or satellite speakers).<\/p>\n<p>The device also has its own digital-to-analog converter. In fact, the Devialet Dione uses the same system on a chip that you can find in the company\u2019s flagship products, the Phantom product line. Devialet has multiple patents for this specific chip and promises a sound with zero background noise, zero saturation and zero distorsion.<\/p>\n<p>And if you\u2019re playing a movie that doesn\u2019t support Dolby Atmos, the Devialet Dione can \u201cupscale\u201d the sound signal to 5.1.2 audio. There\u2019s also a live balance feature that helps you hear dialogue.<\/p>\n<p>When it comes to connectivity, you plug the Devialet Dione to your TV using an HDMI cable with support for eARC and CEC. You can also use the soundbar as a standalone speaker to listen to music.<\/p>\n<p>The Devialet Dione connects to your local network using Wi-Fi or Ethernet. It also supports Bluetooth 5.0 and uses the same Devialet app. You don\u2019t necessarily have to use the app to play some music, as you can use Spotify Connect or AirPlay 2.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2290205\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2290205\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2290205\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg 7500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=150,113 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=300,225 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=768,576 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=680,510 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Devialet-Dione_wall-mount-3_4.jpeg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2290205\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Devialet<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<h2>Not just for audiophiles<\/h2>\n<p>The company thinks there\u2019s a market opportunity with the Devialet Dione as streaming services release blockbuster movies on their services from day one. \u201cWe realized that it\u2019s a market that is taking off,\u201d Lebouchard said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOur typical client is someone who has a beautiful 55-inch TV or bigger. And they want sound quality to be as good as image quality. It\u2019s a bit different from the typical Devialet client, who is someone who listens to a lot of music,\u201d he added.<\/p>\n<p>In 12 months, if the company wants to reach its business goals, the Devialet Dione should represent 20% of the company\u2019s revenue. And every time the startup launches a new product, it can lean on its dense network of points of sale. There are currently 1,900 Devialet points of sale around the world.<\/p>\n<p>While the company has stopped talking about funding rounds since its <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/06\/18\/devialet-maker-of-phantom-speakers-closes-a-20m-series-b-round\/\">Series A in 2015<\/a>, Devialet has raised another \u20ac70 million across two rounds. The last funding round was a \u20ac50 million round with the company\u2019s existing investors in January 2020.<\/p>\n<p>Devialet is launching the Devialet Dione today in France, Belgium, Luxembourg and Switzerland. Pre-orders also start today for other markets.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Meet the Devialet Dione, a brand new speaker from high-end speaker manufacturer Devialet. With this new product, the company is entering a new market \u2014 home cinema sound systems. The Devialet Dione is an all-in-one soundbar compatible with Dolby Atmos 5.1.2 and it costs $2,400 (\u20ac2,190). \u201cWe are at the high end of the market accelerator The Family sues co-founder Oussama Ammar"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.thefamily.co\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Family<\/a> co-founder and CEO Alice Zagury announced <a href=\"https:\/\/salon.thefamily.co\/tomber-et-se-relever-cb9dea4c52b3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a blog post<\/a> that the French startup accelerator is suing Oussama Ammar for multiple claims \u2014\u00a0breach of trust, forgery and use of forgery.<\/p>\n<p>More specifically, Capital <a href=\"https:\/\/www.capital.fr\/economie-politique\/lincubateur-the-family-attaque-en-justice-son-co-fondateur-oussama-ammar-1432210\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">first reported<\/a> that The Family suspects Ammar of diverting \u20ac3 million that was supposed to be invested in several startups through syndicates. TechCrunch has separately seen an email that confirms ongoing charges against Ammar. It was sent to people who transferred money in order to become shareholders in Stripe through a special purpose vehicle. The SPV was supposed to acquire Stripe shares through a secondary offering.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOussama transfers funds to his personal holding companies and tells us after the fact, saying that it\u2019s the only way to take advantage of investment opportunities in question,\u201d Zagury wrote in her blog post.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289842\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>According to her, other people working for The Family have asked several times to see documents that proved that investments went through. In November 2021, Ammar announced on LinkedIn that he was moving on and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:6871047911644418049\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">leaving The Family<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOn Friday, my resignation was published on the Companies House website. From now on I am no longer a director of The Family and I will gradually leave this ecosystem,\u201d Ammar wrote on LinkedIn <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:6871047911644418049\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">at the time<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe ecosystem has changed a lot and raising money is not as difficult as it used to be. It has become normal to raise funds long before you have a product\/market fit, and this poses challenges to entrepreneurs that are of a very different nature than those the ecosystem has faced in the past years,\u201c he added back in November 2021.<\/p>\n<p>Zagury now says that The Family asked him to leave the company in September 2021. \u201cWe bring in a mediator then several law firms as well as an independent auditing firm (PwC),\u201d Zagury wrote.<\/p>\n<p>According to our information, The Family is working with several law firms across several jurisdictions. Capital talked with one of the company\u2019s lawyers, Elsa Sammari. She said that there are multiple ongoing cases being examined by criminal and commercial courts. \u201cThe Family has initiated two proceedings to freeze Oussama Ammar\u2019s assets and the assets of his personal holding companies,\u201d Sammari told Capital.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s not going to be a straightforward case as Ammar\u2019s holding companies are spread all over the world, including in the Cayman Islands and Hong Kong. Ammar also recently edited his <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/oussamaammar\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LinkedIn profile<\/a> saying that he is based in Dubai.<\/p>\n<p>Yesterday, Ammar has reacted to Capital\u2019s report in <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:6913846853348335616\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">another LinkedIn post<\/a>. \u201cThis is a legal proceeding between partners with some lingering resentment. Splitting up like this is a shame but it\u2019s frequent. Entrepreneurs know this well. Since 2020, we have been trying to find an amicable solution. But we haven\u2019t reached an agreement despite long hours of negotiation,\u201d Ammar wrote.<\/p>\n<p>In 2018, Ammar was given <a href=\"https:\/\/www.lexpress.fr\/actualite\/societe\/enquete\/la-face-cachee-d-un-gourou-de-la-tech_2016774.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a four-month suspended sentence<\/a> for a separate case. Back in 2011, Ammar used to work for a company called Be Sport. The company filed a lawsuit for breach of trust, forgery and use of forgery. At the time, Be Sport <a href=\"https:\/\/www.lemonde.fr\/economie\/article\/2018\/05\/07\/oussama-ammar-les-deux-visages-d-un-gourou-de-la-french-tech_5295503_3234.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">claimed<\/a> that Ammar had been using some of the company\u2019s funds for non-corporate expenses.<\/p>\n<p>The Family was originally founded in 2012 with three co-founders \u2014 Alice Zagury, Oussama Ammar and Nicolas Colin. They teamed up to build a different kind of startup accelerator without any batch or demo day. Instead, startups could apply and join the community of startups backed by The Family.<\/p>\n<p>In exchange for a stake, they could get advice from The Family\u2019s team and network with other people in the community. The Family has also helped some of the startups in its community when it comes to fundraising.<\/p>\n<p>Zagury listed some of The Family\u2019s portfolio companies in her blog post. They include Heetch, Algolia, Payfit, Spacefill, Trusk, Northflank, Jow, Joone, Jinka, Doctrine, Merci Handy, So Shape, Side, Vybe, Dark, Unai, WeMaintain, Flat, Fempo, Shipix, MyDiabby, Bellman, Fairmint, Artsper, Caba\u00efa, Plume, Alma and Kymono.<\/p>\n<p>A few years ago, The Family was a cornerstone of the French tech ecosystem. The Family\u2019s office building was a physical representation of a new wave of French startups with global ambitions.<\/p>\n<p>Over time, The Family diversified its activities with an education business and a digital transformation business. In total, The Family has raised \u20ac22 million ($24 million at today\u2019s exchange rate).<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The Family co-founder and CEO Alice Zagury announced in a blog post that the French startup accelerator is suing Oussama Ammar for multiple claims \u2014\u00a0breach of trust, forgery and use of forgery. More specifically, Capital first reported that The Family suspects Ammar of diverting \u20ac3 million that was supposed to be invested in several startups marketplace Malt acquires consulting marketplace Comatch"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It\u2019s consolidation time in the freelancer marketplace industry. French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.malt.fr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Malt<\/a> is acquiring <a href=\"https:\/\/www.comatch.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Comatch<\/a>, a competing marketplace focused on consultants and industry experts. Comatch originally started in Germany, which means that Malt is also doubling down on the German market with this acquisition. Terms of the deal are undisclosed, but it involves a mix of equity and cash.<\/p>\n<p>Malt started as a marketplace that matches freelance developers, designers and other technical workers with companies looking for talent. The startup has raised <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/31\/malt-raises-97m-at-a-489m-valuation-for-its-freelance-marketplace-for-developers\/\">quite a lot of money<\/a> and has managed to attract 340,000 freelancers across multiple European countries.<\/p>\n<p>Originally limited to the French market, Malt has expanded to Germany, Spain, Belgium, the Netherlands and Switzerland over the past few years; 40,000 companies have turned to Malt to find a freelancer or several freelancers.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289084\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Clients include Unilever, Lufthansa, Bosch, BlaBlaCar, L\u2019Or\u00e9al and Allianz. As you can see, a lot of large-sized companies have used Malt at some point.<\/p>\n<p>Malt focuses exclusively on high-skilled freelancing jobs that can fill a gap when a new project comes up. In addition to developers, Malt now also offers opportunities for marketing and communications professionals, graphic designers and more.<\/p>\n<p>Using a platform like Malt can be particularly useful when you\u2019re getting started as a freelancer and you don\u2019t have a big network of potential clients. Malt also helps you take care of the administrative paperwork. Freelancers can charge their clients from Malt directly and, of course, Malt takes a small cut.<\/p>\n<p>As for Comatch, the company roughly follows the same model, but with a specific focus on management consultants and industry experts. Malt hasn\u2019t specifically targeted business consultants so far. So the company is entering a new vertical.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cComatch is a champion in the field of business consulting marketplaces. As a fellow company that shares Malt\u2019s \u2018community first\u2019 approach, placing our talents at the core of the product and business to our vision for the future of work, we are eager and excited to bring our two worlds of high-skilled freelancers together,\u201d Malt co-founder and CEO Vincent Huguet said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>Malt also wants to become the go-to freelancer marketplace in Europe. Comatch has attracted 15,000 freelancers across nine markets and the two companies work with 80% of publicly traded companies on the CAC 40 and DAX 40. Comatch represents an interesting external growth opportunity.<\/p>\n<p>Following this acquisition, Malt has some ambitious goals. By 2024, the company expects to generate \u20ac1 billion in business volume, and it plans to hire another 150 employees by the end of 2022.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ChKsqBZqx2\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/31\/malt-raises-97m-at-a-489m-valuation-for-its-freelance-marketplace-for-developers\/\">Malt raises $97M at a $489M valuation for its freelance marketplace for developers<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Malt raises $97M at a $489M valuation for its freelance marketplace for developers&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/31\/malt-raises-97m-at-a-489m-valuation-for-its-freelance-marketplace-for-developers\/embed\/#?secret=FuEe9jgdpd#?secret=ChKsqBZqx2\" data-secret=\"ChKsqBZqx2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>It\u2019s consolidation time in the freelancer marketplace industry. Comatch originally started in Germany, which means that Malt is also doubling down on the German market with this acquisition. Terms of the deal are undisclosed, but it involves a mix of {"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576630888"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576630888"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576630888"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576630888"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576630888"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":21911,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/marketplace\/","name":"marketplace","slug":"marketplace","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/21911"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=21911"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=21911"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=21911"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=21911"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2289012,"date":"2022-03-25T06:00:19","date_gmt":"2022-03-25T13:00:19","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2289012"},"modified":"2022-03-25T07:46:19","modified_gmt":"2022-03-25T14:46:19","slug":"bigblue-raises-15-million-for-its-d2c-order-fulfillment-service","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/25\/bigblue-raises-15-million-for-its-d2c-order-fulfillment-service\/","title":{"rendered":"Bigblue raises $15 million for its D2C order fulfillment service"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bigblue.co\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bigblue<\/a> has raised a $15 million Series A funding round. The company operates an order fulfillment platform for direct-to-consumer (D2C) brands. In other words, a D2C brand can outsource all things related to logistics to Bigblue so that they can focus on product and marketing.<\/p>\n<p>Runa Capital is leading the round, with LPV acting as the &#8220;secondary lead investor.&#8221; Existing investor Samaipata is also participating once again.<\/p>\n<p>The startup currently operates in three countries \u2014 France, Spain and the U.K. It has signed partnerships with five different warehouses representing over 60,000 square meters of storage space. Bigblue customers can ship their products directly to these warehouses so that they are stored and managed by Bigblue.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289012\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>After that, every time a customer orders something from a Bigblue client, the product is shipped to the end customer using Bigblue\u2019s carrier network. The startup has integrations with more than 20 different carriers and can ship all across Europe \u2014 and even globally, but finding different D2C fulfillment partners in other markets might be a smarter move.<\/p>\n<p>Bigblue lets you customize your packaging and add flyers in the package to personalize the experience for end customers. And if there\u2019s something wrong, customers are invited to file a return request on a branded return portal. It supports store credit as well as refunds.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWith this new round we will support scaling service offerings for Bigblue\u2019s growing base of online merchants, fuel hiring efforts, and continue to position the company as the leader in the D2C fulfillment space,\u201d co-founder and CEO Tim Dumain said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>The result is quite simple. Bigblue wants to offer an Amazon-like experience, but with a third-party logistics stack. Bigblue integrates with many different sales channels, such as Shopify, WooCommerce, PrestaShop, Wix and Magento, as well as various marketplaces on Cdiscount, Fnac and, yes, Amazon.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>It means that you can promise free one-day or two-day deliveries across various marketplaces. And this is key when it comes to getting picked as the main seller on a product page on an online marketplace. Customers also get branded tracking emails.<\/p>\n<p>The startup competes with other D2C e-commerce logistics companies, such as <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cubyn.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cubyn<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hive.app\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hive<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.huboo.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Huboo<\/a>. Overall, Bigblue has managed to attract 300 customers, such as <a href=\"https:\/\/en.fromfuture.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">From Future<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/unbottled.co\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Unbottled<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/wearejolies.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">We Are Jolies<\/a>. The company plans to ship 4 million parcels this year. Over the next 12 months, the startup plans to hire another 100 employees and expand across Western Europe.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup Bigblue has raised a $15 million Series A funding round. The company operates an order fulfillment platform for direct-to-consumer (D2C) brands. In other words, a D2C brand can outsource all things related to logistics to Bigblue so that they can focus on product and marketing. Runa Capital is leading the round, with LPV
