g","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560098"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560098"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560098"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560098"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560098"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2287972,"date":"2022-03-24T01:00:04","date_gmt":"2022-03-24T08:00:04","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287972"},"modified":"2022-03-24T06:00:56","modified_gmt":"2022-03-24T13:00:56","slug":"weglot-raises-50-million-to-turn-any-website-into-a-multilingual-site","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/24\/weglot-raises-50-million-to-turn-any-website-into-a-multilingual-site\/","title":{"rendered":"Weglot raises $50 million to turn any website into a multilingual site"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/weglot.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Weglot<\/a> has closed a $50 million Series A funding round (\u20ac45 million) from <a href=\"https:\/\/partechpartners.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Partech<\/a>. The company has built a translation solution for websites. It helps you add more languages to your site without a lot of tweaking and without having to switch to a different CMS or e-commerce platform.<\/p>\n<p>And this is key to understanding Weglot\u2019s positioning. Translation plugins for WordPress of Shopify have been around for a while. But Weglot wants to build a universal product that works for all sorts of web experiences.<\/p>\n<p>There are two ways to take advantage of Weglot. You can add it to your existing website with a plugin \u2014 this is how Weglot works with WordPress, Shopify, Wix and WooCommerce. If you run a small company and don\u2019t have a dedicated web developer, you could install Weglot without writing any line of code.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287972\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The other way is that you can add a few lines of Javascript to the <code>&lt;head&gt;<\/code> tag of your website. Weglot uses this approach for Webflow, Squarespace and BigCommerce. You also need to tweak your DNS records to create subdomains or subdirectories for new languages.<\/p>\n<p>On Weglot\u2019s servers, the company automatically detects and pulls content from the site. Weglot customers can use automatic translation to get started with new languages.<\/p>\n<p>The company also offers a dashboard so that you can dive into your content and create better translations. You can grant access to professional translators and manage translations from that interface.<\/p>\n<p>After that, you have a multilingual site. Whenever a visitor loads your site, the website will load in their preferred language by default. You can also add a language switcher in the corner of your website if you want to offer multiple options.<\/p>\n<p>Even though translations are stored on Weglot\u2019s servers, Weglot creates dedicated subdirectories or subdomains for each language. This way, Google and other search engines can index each language variant of your website. Metadata and keywords can also be translated with Weglot.<\/p>\n<p>The startup charges a <a href=\"https:\/\/weglot.com\/pricing\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">monthly subscription<\/a> depending on the number of languages and words that you need. Last year, Weglot has reached $11 million (\u20ac10 million) in annual recurring revenue. Not bad for a startup that hasn\u2019t raised any outside capital since its seed round in 2017.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup Weglot has closed a $50 million Series A funding round (\u20ac45 million) from Partech. The company has built a translation solution for websites. It helps you add more languages to your site without a lot of tweaking and without having to switch to a different CMS or e-commerce platform. And this is key modified":"2022-03-21T07:51:24","modified_gmt":"2022-03-21T14:51:24","slug":"lune-offers-an-api-to-calculate-carbon-emissions-at-checkout","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/20\/lune-offers-an-api-to-calculate-carbon-emissions-at-checkout\/","title":{"rendered":"Lune offers an API to calculate carbon emissions at checkout"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Meet <a href=\"https:\/\/lune.co\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lune<\/a>, a new startup that wants to expose CO2 emissions calculations so that customers are better informed when they purchase something online. When companies start using Lune\u2019s API, they can also let their customers pay a fee to finance a carbon neutralization project.<\/p>\n<p>Before founding Lune with Roberto Bruggemann, Erik Stadigh previously worked for VC fund <a href=\"https:\/\/crane.vc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Crane<\/a>, which led Lune&#8217;s $4 million seed round. In addition, 15 business angels &#8212; including N26 co-founder Maximilian Tayenthal, Voi co-founder Fredrik Hjelm, and OysterHR and Nexmo co-founder Tony Jamous &#8212;\u00a0participated.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe way things work today is that companies create a sustainability report that is hidden away on the website and very few people read it,\u201d co-founder Stadigh told me.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286596\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The startup first helps you measure the carbon impact. As always, those are just estimations. \u201cWe offer automated carbon emission calculations and follow best practice guidelines,\u201d Stadigh said.<\/p>\n<p>And once you integrate the API in your product, customers can choose to pay a bit more to contribute to compensation projects. \u201cWe partner with carbon offset developers across the world,\u201d Stadigh said.<\/p>\n<p>Lune also works directly with payment companies, such as TrueLayer. When it\u2019s time to check out, customers can choose a \u201cgreen payment method\u201d that will contribute to carbon offset projects.<\/p>\n<p>From the merchant\u2019s perspective, Lune customers can choose to pay for those projects or let customers pay the extra fee. Lune is already talking with other payment partners to offer more payment integrations.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Lune charges based on the number of calculations and also takes a small cut on carbon offsetting transactions. With Lune\u2019s API, the startup wants to turn any company into a climate-friendly company.<\/p>\n<p>Many would say that not purchasing a product is the best way to reduce the carbon impact of that potential purchase. But when you can\u2019t avoid a purchase, it could help customers pick one company over another.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286600\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286600\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286600\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"444\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg 2880w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=150,65 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=300,130 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=768,333 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=680,295 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=1536,666 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=2048,887 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Lune-team.jpeg?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286600\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Lune<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Meet Lune, a new startup that wants to expose CO2 emissions calculations so that customers are better informed when they purchase something online. d-companies?tags=576995923"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576995923"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576995923"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2286124,"date":"2022-03-17T09:43:11","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T16:43:11","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2286124"},"modified":"2022-03-17T11:57:04","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T18:57:04","slug":"amie-is-a-new-calendar-app-with-a-social-twist","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/amie-is-a-new-calendar-app-with-a-social-twist\/","title":{"rendered":"Amie is a new calendar app with a social twist"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Meet <a href=\"https:\/\/amie.so\">Amie<\/a>, a startup working on a brand new productivity app for both individuals and teams. The company is unveiling its app this week and users can sign up to the waitlist. Amie is a well-designed calendar app that helps you get things done and keep up with your team.<\/p>\n<p>Amie was founded by Dennis M\u00fcller, who previously worked as a product manager for challenger bank <a href=\"https:\/\/n26.com\">N26<\/a>. Creandum, as well as Tiny.VC and several business angels, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/09\/amie\/\">backed the company<\/a> early on so that it could work on its product without too much pressure.<\/p>\n<p>And what I saw during a demo with M\u00fcller was a polished app that could easily attract a loyal user base. There are a lot of tiny details that make it much more convenient than the default option for many companies, which is Google Calendar.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286124\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>When you open Amie, it looks like a calendar, there\u2019s no question about it. You can see the current week with all your events, click on an event to get details and move from one week to another.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286126\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286126\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286126\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"666\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png 1080w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=150,98 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=300,195 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=768,499 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=680,442 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/calendar-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286126\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Amie<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But Amie is quite opinionated in its feature set, and especially around todo items. You can open your todo list in a column right next to your calendar and view them this way. But you can also drag them from the sidebar and drop them in the main calendar view to assign a date and time to your todo.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIf you want to achieve something, the easiest way to do it is put it in your calendar, assign a time to it,\u201d M\u00fcller told me. And it\u2019s true that many people already use their calendar as a sort of todo list already. The fact that todos can live in the sidebar or in your week view gives more flexibility than adding your todos to your calendar directly.<\/p>\n<p>In the left-side column, you can also see a list of avatars. If you\u2019re using Slack intensively, it looks a bit like the icons on the left to switch from one workspace to another.<\/p>\n<p>In Amie\u2019s case, those icons represent other people in your team. Like in instant messengers, you can see if they\u2019re currently available or busy based on their calendar. And if you hover over their avatar, you can toggle their calendar. For instance, it\u2019s a good way to find out when it would be a good time to set up a meeting.<\/p>\n<p>Each person also gets their own profile. On this separate page, you can see what someone is doing right now, get a reminder about their birthday, add a few notes and view when was the last time you were together. You can also set recurring reminders. It\u2019s a lightweight feature that could help you stay in touch with people more regularly.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286127\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286127\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286127\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"666\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png 1080w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=150,98 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=300,195 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=768,499 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=680,442 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/profiles-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286127\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Amie<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>You also get some information from third-party services. For instance, you can see the current song playing from this person\u2019s Spotify account. You can also open their Twitter profile from there.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThese calendar apps that are really focused on one person are cool. But if you look at other products that are successful today and if you want to generate some kind of network effects, we realized that we had to build some kind of profile,\u201d M\u00fcller told me.<\/p>\n<p>The instant benefit of adding a social component to the calendar is that you can more easily stay on top of the company\u2019s activities. Amie has a home view with an activity feed. On this screen, you can see when someone creates an event.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s full of information and it could be particularly useful for companies with a transparent culture. \u201cThe home view could become the modern intranet,\u201d M\u00fcller said.<\/p>\n<p>On this home view, you can also see a list of all your events and todos. You can check things off from this view.<\/p>\n<p>Finally, Amie has many of the power features that you would expect from a modern productivity tool. With just a keyboard shortcut, you can open a quick action menu, create an event, move to another view, etc.<\/p>\n<p>When you want to share your availabilities with someone else, you can choose some slots in your calendar and share a link with the other person \u2014\u00a0no Calendly required. When an event is coming up with a video call, you can join the call with a keyboard shortcut.<\/p>\n<p>Amie currently works with Google accounts on macOS and Windows. There\u2019s also an iPhone app and the company is working on an Android app as well. On mobile, Amie has tried to locate all the important buttons and gestures near the bottom of the screen so that you don\u2019t have to move your hand to reach a button in the corner.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019re currently experiencing a calendar renaissance. Many startups are trying to find the right formula to reinvent the calendar app for the Notion era. Amie competes with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/28\/rise-is-a-new-calendar-app-with-a-scheduling-engine-for-teams\/\">Rise<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/18\/cron-is-a-new-calendar-app-following-in-sunrises-footsteps\/\">Cron<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/25\/hera-is-a-new-calendar-app-for-people-with-a-lot-of-virtual-meetings\/\">Hera<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/08\/fantastical-lets-you-share-a-link-to-schedule-meetings-no-calendly-required\/\">Fantastical<\/a> and others.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s arguably a big market. So it\u2019s good to see so much innovation in the space. \u201cFor us, the calendar is the canvas,\u201d M\u00fcller told me. \u201cWe do our job right if you sign up and you never open Google Calendar again.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286125\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286125\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286125\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"666\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png 1080w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=150,98 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=300,195 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=768,499 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=680,442 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/booking-page-\u2013-for-romain.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286125\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Amie<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PeA6qnIIQC\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/09\/amie\/\">Creandum backs Amie, a new productivity app from ex-N26 product manager Dennis M\u00fcller<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285930"},"modified":"2022-03-17T07:29:00","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T14:29:00","slug":"galion-exe-is-a-new-paris-based-seed-fund","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/galion-exe-is-a-new-paris-based-seed-fund\/","title":{"rendered":"Galion.exe is a new Paris-based seed fund"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">There\u2019s a new seed fund in town, but with a familiar name. <a href=\"https:\/\/thegalionproject.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Galion<\/a>, a collective of tech entrepreneurs who network and learn from each other, is launching an investment arm called <a href=\"https:\/\/galion.exe.vc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Galion.exe<\/a>. They have already raised \u20ac30 million ($33 million at today\u2019s exchange rate) and aim to reach a total fund size of \u20ac60 to \u20ac80 million ($66 million to $88 million).<\/p>\n<p>Originally founded in 2015, The Galion Project started as a sort of think tank for the tech community. For instance, they came up with a template for a fair term sheet.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cJean-Baptiste Rudelle was convinced that we would have more unicorns in the French tech ecosystem,\u201d Galion co-founder and CEO Agathe Wautier told me. \u201cThe goal was to share as much as possible to think bigger and go faster. Very quickly, we created the think tank. We put together a knowledge base with several reports and tools for entrepreneurs, made by entrepreneurs.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285930\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>That project is still going well as there are currently 400 active members in the Galion community. In order to join this community, you have to prove that you have raised at least \u20ac3 million, you need to be invited by two Galion peers and you need to pay \u20ac2,000 every year.<\/p>\n<p>But very quickly, some entrepreneurs in the community became business angels. Some of them wanted to work together on deals and form syndicates.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAt some point, there was so much demand that we thought we had to do something ourselves,\u201d Wautier said.<\/p>\n<p>Around the same time, Willy Braun and Kevin Kuipers left another Paris-based VC fund, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.daphni.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Daphni<\/a>. Chlo\u00e9 Monneyron joined the pair as an associate VC and they all started working on Galion&#8217;s investment fund.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>They first started raising Galion.exe from the Galion community. I\u2019m told the barrier to entry was quite low as you could participate in the fund with the minimum legal amount for this kind of investment.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to those individual investors, Galion.exe will round up its fund with more traditional limited partners, such as institutional investors, family offices, private banks, etc.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhen we left Daphni, we had a strong thesis on seed rounds. When you look at the amount and number of deals, everything has doubled from Series A rounds and beyond,\u201d Braun told me. But the same isn\u2019t necessarily true for seed rounds.<\/p>\n<p>Galion.exe now plans to invest in a dozen companies every year and fill that seed gap in France. The team will be able to invest anything between \u20ac700,000 and \u20ac2.5 million so that they can lead the seed round without any co-investor (even though they don\u2019t exclude co-investments altogether).<\/p>\n<p>\u201cFor the first time, seed-stage companies will be able to join the Galion community,\u201d Kuipers told me.<\/p>\n<p>And that could be a win-win for everyone involved. Portfolio companies will be able to learn from peers, get introductions and apply some best practices. And Galion.exe could convince early-stage startups to sign a term sheet with them based on that argument alone.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>There\u2019s a new seed fund in town, but with a familiar name. Galion, a collective of tech entrepreneurs who network and learn from each other, is launching an investment arm called Galion.exe. They have already raised \u20ac30 million ($33 million at today\u2019s exchange rate) and aim to reach a total fund size of \u20ac60 to He has helped several non-profit organizations, such as StartHer, an organization that promotes education and empowerment of women in technology, and Techfugees, an organization that empowers displaced people with technology.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Disclosure: Romain owns small amounts of various is now worth nearly $12 billion after raising another $768 million"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Instant delivery startup <a href=\"https:\/\/getir.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Getir<\/a> announced that it has closed a new $768 million Series E funding round. Following this deal, the company reached a valuation of $11.8 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Mubadala Investment Company is leading the round, with Abu Dhabi Growth Fund (ADG), Alpha Wave Global, Sequoia Capital and Tiger Global also participating.<\/p>\n<p>Originally from Turkey, Getir has quickly expanded its service across Europe and the U.S. Unlike traditional grocery delivery services, Getir lets your order groceries without having to pick a delivery slot. As soon as you send your order, Getir starts working on it.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285915\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Behind the scenes, Getir has built dense networks of micro-fulfillment centers in dozens of urban areas. Those dark stores are operated by Getir and the company also controls and owns the inventory of products.<\/p>\n<p>After that, a delivery person on a bike or moped scooter delivers your order as quickly as possible. It means that you can expect to receive your order in \u201cminutes,\u201d the company\u2019s website says. More realistically, you should get it 20 to 40 minutes later.<\/p>\n<p>The company has managed to attract 40 million app downloads across nine countries. Overall, Getir manages 1,100 dark stores. That\u2019s why these instant delivery startups have been raising mega-rounds of funding &#8212; it\u2019s a capital-intensive industry.<\/p>\n<p>Getir is quite dominant in Turkey, currently operating in 81 cities. The company covers 48 cities for all other markets \u2014 the U.K., Germany, France, Italy, Spain, Netherlands, Portugal and the U.S.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are defining the ultrafast delivery sector and this latest round of funding is a testament to Getir\u2019s position as industry pioneer. In such an exciting and competitive market we cannot afford to stand still. This investment will enable us to further develop our proposition and technology, as well as invest in our employees to continue to attract the best talent,\u201d Getir founder Nazim Salur said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>The company competes with <a href=\"https:\/\/gopuff.com\/go\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gopuff<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.goflink.com\/en\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Flink<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/gorillas.io\/en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gorillas<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/tryzapp.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zapp<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cajoo.eu\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cajoo<\/a> and more. In other words, it\u2019s an incredibly crowded market, and there will be more consolidation moves down the road.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"49IyTn5afZ\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/gopuff-officially-launches-its-instant-delivery-service-in-france\/\">Gopuff officially launches its instant delivery service in France<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Gopuff officially launches its instant delivery service in France&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/gopuff-officially-launches-its-instant-delivery-service-in-france\/embed\/#?secret=BLGK7P6Ojj#?secret=49IyTn5afZ\" data-secret=\"49IyTn5afZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Instant delivery startup Getir announced that it has closed a new $768 million Series E funding round. grabs $5 million for its real-time collaboration API"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/liveblocks.io\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Liveblocks<\/a> has raised a $5 million seed round. The startup lets you turn a regular web app into a multiplayer product with high-level hosted APIs. In addition to its live presence state API, the company is launching its live storage API.<\/p>\n<p>Boldstart is leading today\u2019s round. Atlassian, Kima Ventures, Seedcamp as well as multiple business angels also participated. Boldstart and Seedcamp already invested in the company\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/16\/liveblocks-is-an-api-that-lets-you-add-real-time-collaboration-to-your-product\/\">pre-seed round<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Over the past few years, building a web app has become easier thanks to frameworks and APIs. But letting multiple people interact with the same document, form, whiteboard or piece of content is still incredibly hard.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2276412\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Liveblocks essentially helps you get there faster. The startup first released a live presence state API. When you open a document in Google Docs, you can see several profile pictures in the top-right corner. It tells you who is viewing a document right now. And you can see if someone else is moving their cursor or selecting some text.<\/p>\n<p>When you integrate Liveblocks\u2019 presence API, you can take advantage of the API to display the list of people currently viewing a document just like in Google Docs. It can also track everyone\u2019s cursors in real time.<\/p>\n<p>While this is somewhat useful, the startup has been working on another API that opens up a lot of possibilities. With its live storage API, several people can view and edit data simultaneously. It can be used to create collaborative whiteboards, a note-taking app, a multiplayer CMS, etc.<\/p>\n<p>The hardest part of real-time data collaboration is conflict resolution. Liveblocks tries to minimize issues with offline support, and multiplayer undo and redo. If you\u2019re using a library like Zustand or Redux, you can integrate Liveblocks so that multiple users can interact with data at the same time.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Over the past three months, the total number of connections to Liveblocks rooms have increased by 10x. And this metric should increase rapidly as remote work and software-as-a-service products become more popular.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"LJw6tzFDft\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/16\/liveblocks-is-an-api-that-lets-you-add-real-time-collaboration-to-your-product\/\">Liveblocks is an API that lets you add real-time collaboration to your product<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Liveblocks is an API that lets you add real-time collaboration to your product&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/16\/liveblocks-is-an-api-that-lets-you-add-real-time-collaboration-to-your-product\/embed\/#?secret=kcQwmKNjrK#?secret=LJw6tzFDft\" data-secret=\"LJw6tzFDft\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Liveblocks has raised a $5 million seed round. The startup lets you turn a regular web app into a multiplayer product with high-level hosted APIs. In addition to its live presence state API, the company is launching its live storage API. helps companies build flexible logistics networks"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/spacefill.fr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SpaceFill<\/a> has raised a $27 million funding round (\u20ac25 million) led by NGP Capital with Maersk Growth and existing investors Eurazeo and La Famiglia also participating. The company is building a warehousing cloud across several European countries that offers both flexibility and transparency.<\/p>\n<p>SpaceFill doesn\u2019t work with e-commerce companies trying to store goods before shipping them to customers. Instead, the company focuses exclusively on the B2B side of the industry, which is arguably the larger side of the industry. You could compare SpaceFill to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.flexe.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Flexe<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.stord.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stord<\/a> \u2014 but SpaceFill focuses on Europe.<\/p>\n<p>The company has built a network of 1,500 warehouses that are all connected to the same software orchestrating layer. This software layer acts as\u00a0a sort of control tower for your inventory and logistics strategy.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284063\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Those warehouses are third-party logistics providers that have chosen to allocate part of their warehousing space to SpaceFill customers. They can still accept their own customers, but they can more easily fill up the rest of their warehouses thanks to SpaceFill.<\/p>\n<p>On the other side, SpaceFill acts as a long-term logistics partner. Instead of working with a traditional logistics outsourcing company, SpaceFill becomes your logistics partner.<\/p>\n<p>Customers can leverage SpaceFill\u2019s network for cross-docking operations, which means that a truck can drop several goods in a warehouse so that multiple trucks can pick up a smaller quantity of those goods and move them to another location.<\/p>\n<p>SpaceFill also handles variations in capacity needs, which can be particularly useful for your seasonality strategy. Just like cloud storage, you can easily store more goods (and pay more), or reduce your storage capacity when you need less warehousing space.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIn the logistics industry, the tech stack is super old and super hard to interconnect,\u201d co-founder and CEO Maxime Huzar told me. \u201cWe have built a sort of power adapter that connects with the entire network.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>SpaceFill currently serves 500 customers, such as Ikea, Angell Bike and Leroy Merlin. It has 60 employees and generates more than \u20ac10 million in revenue. The company plans to hire another 80 employees to improve its platform and expand its network.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup SpaceFill has raised a $27 million funding round (\u20ac25 million) led by NGP Capital with Maersk Growth and existing investors Eurazeo and La Famiglia also participating. The company is building a warehousing cloud across several European countries that offers both flexibility and transparency. SpaceFill doesn\u2019t work with e-commerce companies trying to store goods ":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":42020,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/warehouse\/","name":"warehouse","slug":"warehouse","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/42020"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=42020"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=42020"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=42020"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=42020"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284915,"date":"2022-03-15T12:40:16","date_gmt":"2022-03-15T19:40:16","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284915"},"modified":"2022-03-15T16:04:41","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T23:04:41","slug":"ukraines-mykhailo-fedorov-talks-about-corporate-sanctions-and-running-a-government-during-wartime","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/ukraines-mykhailo-fedorov-talks-about-corporate-sanctions-and-running-a-government-during-wartime\/","title":{"rendered":"Ukraine\u2019s Mykhailo Fedorov talks about corporate sanctions and running a government during wartime"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The Russian army<\/span> started invading Ukraine three weeks ago. And the conflict has been multifaceted from day one. In addition to the ground war, the Ukrainian government quickly reacted on the digital front. Representatives asked for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/how-ukraine-is-spending-crypto-donations\/\">cryptocurrency donations<\/a>, called out tech companies so that they would <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ukraine-war\/\">suspend<\/a> sales and services in Russia and organized a digital resistance.<\/p>\n<p>One of the public figures that embody the government\u2019s reaction to the Russian invasion is Mykhailo Fedorov. In 2019, he became Ukraine\u2019s first minister of Digital Transformation at the age of 28. He is also the vice prime minister of Ukraine. The country\u2019s deputy minister for Digital Transformation Oleksandr (Alex) Bornyakov has also played an important part in Ukraine&#8217;s government \u2014 TechCrunch&#8217;s Ingrid Lunden <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/ukraine-deputy-minister-talks-it-army-and-deploying-25m-in-donated-crypto\/\">interviewed Bornyakov last week<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOur vision with President Zelensky \u2014 before the war \u2014 was to build the world\u2019s most convenient country in terms of digitally available public services,\u201d Mykhailo Fedorov said in an interview with TechCrunch earlier today.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284915\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>While many of those projects are currently on hold, the Ukrainian government already sees the benefits of its digital transformation efforts. Fedorov is also very active on the digital diplomacy front. He is well aware that Big Tech companies have become quite powerful when it comes to international relations. That\u2019s why he is doing whatever he can to have them on Ukraine\u2019s side.<\/p>\n<p>In a wide-ranging interview on Zoom and with the help of a translator, Fedorov also shared some insights about what it\u2019s like to participate in a government during wartime. The interview has been slightly edited for clarity and brevity.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><strong>TechCrunch: Where are you right now? Can you tell us about your current personal situation?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><strong>Mykhailo Fedorov:<\/strong> I\u2019m at the very center of action. I can\u2019t quite give you a geolocation for security reasons but let me assure you we stay in touch with the president\u2019s team 24\/7 about all the projects.<\/p>\n<p><strong>I\u2019m sure your daily life is very different right now from what it was a couple of months ago. Can you tell us about your day-to-day job and role during the war against Russia?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>We are a very young ministry. We have been created by President Zelensky when he was elected to implement some crucial parts of his program. Before the election I was the head of his digital campaign. After he got elected, we joined forces to implement our shared vision of a digital country.<\/p>\n<p>And our vision with President Zelensky \u2014 before the war \u2014 was to build the world\u2019s most convenient country in terms of digitally available public services. And our goal was to create a government where services would be available in a double tap. They would be semi-automated with as little interference with public officials as possible. In other words, we tried to be more resemblant of an Uber than a government as you would expect it to be.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Is there any way you can leverage those digital public services to help Ukrainians during this time of crisis?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>We have created something like a factory to launch public services. That\u2019s enabled by our app which has 15 million users. And it\u2019s also enabled by the interactions of all of the government-run databases that we\u2019ve been able to implement through this period of time, and also by our management structure, which has been fine-tuned to basically launch new services and provide these things.<\/p>\n<p>For example, during wartime, we\u2019ve been able to launch such services as cash payouts to people who have been forced to resettle from areas that were badly affected by combat. Also, we\u2019ve been able to embed free public television and free radio. We also added the possibility to raise money for the army through official channels.<\/p>\n<p>We have services that allow us to track and report on the enemy movements as well. It\u2019s basically crowdsourced intelligence, and we\u2019ve been able to launch that in just a couple of days since the war erupted.<\/p>\n<p>Because our internal ID is a very specific document and not everybody has it. But during war time, we\u2019ve been able to launch an additional document that has all of the vital information for internal mobility and getting public services no matter who you are and where you are and what your status is. We\u2019re also working on a service to basically provide an inventory of your property if it has been damaged or destroyed by the war for future processes.<\/p>\n<p><strong>These services imply that you can get a good connection to internet services where you are right now. What\u2019s the current status of both cellular and landline connectivity?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>I would say that we are very stable and confident at the moment because of our telecom industry. I think they are real heroes because they work around the clock. And whenever there\u2019s an outage, they go out and fix it.<\/p>\n<p>So we are able to maintain stable internet connectivity throughout most of the country. We also have the largest number of Starlink terminals anywhere in the EU.<\/p>\n<p><strong>What\u2019s the plan for sensitive data that you hold from both the army and the government? Is data based in Ukraine right now? And do you have plans to relocate data to foreign countries to prepare for a worst case scenario?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Building a digital state increases your exposure, your surface of attack, which means that we have been always very mindful and very serious about cybersecurity. Also, as we we have been building our digital state, we have been constantly targeted by the Russian Federation with cyber attacks.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tI think that, in the future, governments will resemble tech companies, not classical governments.\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<cite>Mykhailo Fedorov<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p>Without elaborating, I would like to say that our data is safe. We have backups. We have means to ensure consistency and safety of the data. This means that our services will remain reliable and available for Ukrainian citizens no matter what happens.<\/p>\n<p><strong>I want to change the topic and talk about corporate sanctions against Russia, because you\u2019ve been calling out companies on Twitter and in media outlets saying that companies from Europe and North America should suspend sales in Russia right now. Where does this idea come from and do you think it\u2019s effective?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>We call this project digital blockade. And we believe that this is a very crucial component to winning this war. And I think that, in the future, governments will resemble tech companies, not classical governments.<\/p>\n<p>Digital platforms provide some vital services. They have become so embedded into the fabric of society. Once you start removing these services from the aggressor, one by one, you actually damage their fabric of society and you make it very uncomfortable for them to go along with their daily lives.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019d like to think of this as a completely new and unexplored battlefield. And this is a complementary measure to sanctions which we expect is going to push the development of Russia back decades.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tWhen you create these unfavorable conditions in Russia, you&#8217;re likely to cause the tech talent to move elsewhere.\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<cite>Mykhailo Fedorov<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p>I also think that high-tech businesses create tremendous added value. And that\u2019s why Tesla is worth more than Gazprom. People who create this added value, the tech talent, they\u2019re actually very mobile and nomadic. When you create these unfavorable conditions in Russia, you\u2019re likely to cause the tech talent to move elsewhere.<\/p>\n<p>This is why we are committed to making this digital blockade as thorough and as comprehensive as we can. Up until the moment when Russian tanks and soldiers leave our country and stop killing our people.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Are there some companies that haven\u2019t done enough in your opinion and should do more to suspend sales and stop doing business in Russia?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>I think one company I\u2019d particularly like to call out is SAP. It\u2019s a German company that provides ERP to banks and major enterprises. Basically, they contribute to the aggressive war by providing IT infrastructure to Russian companies and also by paying taxes in Russia. Thus, they support the army that is murdering Ukrainian nationals and civilians.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Can you talk about the tech industry and tech community in Ukraine right now? Because obviously we tend to cover a lot of what\u2019s happening in the tech community and we would like to know how tech talent in Ukraine is reacting right now.<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>There are about 300,000 tech talent in Ukraine. Most of these international companies have been able to stabilize their operations and ensure business continuity in Ukraine. Even though it\u2019s been challenging but most of them are managing to do it.<\/p>\n<p>We try to cater to the needs of our tech companies by providing them with broadband internet, with safe locations, with some tax stimulus, as well as with mobility. So basically, we aim to be their one-stop shop \u2014 should they have problems.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yesterday, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-ukraine-has-started-using-clearview-ais-facial-recognition-during-war-2022-03-13\/\">a report<\/a> came out saying that the Ukrainian army has been using Clearview AI\u2019s facial recognition technology. Can you tell us more about this partnership with Clearview AI?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>I would say that this project is currently in very early development. I would not be in a position to comment on the progress but once we have results I would be glad to share results.<\/p>\n<p><strong>What kind of use cases do you have in mind when leveraging Clearview AI?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>I would start off by saying that most of these use cases would not be public, not something that we\u2019d be able to share publicly.<\/p>\n<p>But something that I can just give you a sneak peek would be our work with the Ministry of Internal Affairs. We would be trying to identify Russian forces who have been killed or taken prisoner in Ukraine. As you know, the Russian government starts to deny their presence, send them without documents, etc.<\/p>\n<p>Another one would be checking people who cross our roadblocks. Another one would be looking for missing persons.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"hEkiVGTBEd\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/ukraine-deputy-minister-talks-it-army-and-deploying-25m-in-donated-crypto\/\">Ukraine deputy minister talks IT Army and deploying $25M in donated crypto<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Ukraine deputy minister talks IT Army and deploying $25M in donated crypto&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/ukraine-deputy-minister-talks-it-army-and-deploying-25m-in-donated-crypto\/embed\/#?secret=6XRTKOIVQi#?secret=hEkiVGTBEd\" data-secret=\"hEkiVGTBEd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><strong>I want to ask you about cryptocurrency donations as well. Can you give us an update on your strategy when it comes to cryptocurrencies?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>As of now, we have been able to raise $55 million. And all of that has been directed toward the needs of the Ukrainian army.<\/p>\n<p>We are also trying to become a crypto friendly country. I can even give you some specifics. The Parliament has adopted a law on virtual assets. I think the president is about to sign it into law in a matter of days. So we strive to be as friendly to virtual assets as possible. And we are continuing this effort during war time as well.<\/p>\n<p><strong>You talked about passing a new law on cryptocurrencies in Ukraine. How does it work tight now as a government member? How do you pass new laws and how do you work as a team with the rest of the government?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s an excellent question. During wartime our government is working in overdrive mode basically. We\u2019re working 24\/7 \u2014 no weekends. While our cabinet meetings were held weekly before the war now they\u2019re held daily.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tI&#8217;d like to say thank you to the entire tech community because I believe that the tech community has chosen our side.\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<cite>Mykhailo Fedorov<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p>Just like the brave servicemen and women in our armed forces are defending our country day and night without any weekends or holidays. We\u2019re doing likewise.<\/p>\n<p>We are working on the military front; we are working on the tech front. We are also working on the economic front. And our government has been working especially hard to liberalize the economy and remove all hurdles, roadblocks and bottlenecks in our economy. We are simplifying tax rules. We are opening up our customs and \u2014 gee \u2014 we\u2019re even trying to develop our country economically despite the war.<\/p>\n<p><strong>I think I\u2019ve asked everything I wanted to know about the current state. If you\u2019re willing we can talk regularly every week or every couple of weeks to share an update. But for now, I want to thank you for your answers.<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Sure I\u2019d like to organize a follow-up call. And I\u2019d like to also just say a few words in conclusion, if you could put those in your article.<\/p>\n<p>I\u2019d like to say thank you to the entire tech community because I believe that the tech community has chosen our side, which is obviously the side of good. We can feel it with our hearts and we can feel it by the actions of the tech community, and we are very grateful for that.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The Russian army started invading Ukraine three weeks ago. war","slug":"ukraine-war","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576989147"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576989147"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576989147"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576989147"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576989147"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284514,"date":"2022-03-15T02:56:41","date_gmt":"2022-03-15T09:56:41","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284514"},"modified":"2022-03-15T10:52:17","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T17:52:17","slug":"healthcare-tech-platform-doctolib-reaches-6-4-billion-valuation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/healthcare-tech-platform-doctolib-reaches-6-4-billion-valuation\/","title":{"rendered":"Healthcare tech platform Doctolib reaches $6.4 billion valuation"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.doctolib.fr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Doctolib<\/a> has <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/pulse\/500-millions-deuros-pour-cr%C3%A9er-3-emplois-et-renforcer-niox-chateau\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced<\/a> that is has raised a new funding round. With this round, the company has reached a valuation of \u20ac5.8 billion, or $6.4 billion at today\u2019s exchange rate. That makes Doctolib the highest valued French startup.<\/p>\n<p>The startup says it has raised $549 million (\u20ac500 million) in both equity and debt. Eurazeo is leading the round, with Bpifrance and General Atlantic also participating in the round \u2014 they also invested in the company&#8217;s previous rounds.<\/p>\n<p>In case you\u2019re not familiar with Doctolib, the company\u2019s main product is a software-as-a-service platform for doctors and medical workers. The company wants to help them tackle admin tasks. In particular, Doctolib acts as a booking platform that connects doctors with patients; 60 million people have used it in France, Germany and Italy.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284514\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>With today\u2019s funding round, the company plans to grow from 2,500 employees to 6,000 employees over the next five years. Doctolib relies on a vast network of offices in major and mid-sized European cities so that they can talk with doctors all around France, Germany and Italy. Doctolib plans to operate across 30 cities.<\/p>\n<p>In January, Doctolib talked about <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/10\/doctolib-is-now-used-by-300000-doctors-and-medical-workers\/\">its roadmap<\/a> for 2022 and beyond. The company plans to create a suite of products and expand beyond appointment booking.<\/p>\n<p>And the company has already added some new SaaS products, just like Salesforce is always iterating on its suite of products. In addition to a telehealth add-on, the startup has a product called <a href=\"https:\/\/info.doctolib.fr\/doctolib-medecin\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Doctolib M\u00e9decin<\/a> that can help you centralize documents, see a patient\u2019s history, take notes and issue invoices.<\/p>\n<p>With <a href=\"https:\/\/info.doctolib.fr\/doctolib-team\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Doctolib Team<\/a>, the company is creating an instant messaging service for health professionals. They could use the service to securely talk about patients and send documents.<\/p>\n<p>As Doctolib operates in a highly sensitive industry, the company has also been investing in security and privacy. Doctolib acquired Tanker, as <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/11\/healthcare-tech-platform-doctolib-acquires-encryption-startup-tanker\/\">I first reported<\/a>. Tanker is a turnkey solution that helps you enable end-to-end encryption in a medical application.<\/p>\n<p>Overall, 300,000 healthcare workers are using Doctolib \u2014 not all of them pay for a monthly subscription. The startup also works with 250 public hospitals. And if you\u2019re living in France, you know that Doctolib has become ubiquitous.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PdgeN5enu9\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/11\/healthcare-tech-platform-doctolib-acquires-encryption-startup-tanker\/\">Healthcare tech platform Doctolib acquires encryption startup Tanker<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Healthcare tech platform Doctolib acquires encryption startup Tanker&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/11\/healthcare-tech-platform-doctolib-acquires-encryption-startup-tanker\/embed\/#?secret=wa9wNPWAVN#?secret=PdgeN5enu9\" data-secret=\"PdgeN5enu9\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"edXwIkzxvL\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/10\/doctolib-is-now-used-by-300000-doctors-and-medical-workers\/\">Doctolib is now used by 300,000 doctors and medical workers<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Doctolib is now used by 300,000 doctors and medical workers&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/10\/doctolib-is-now-used-by-300000-doctors-and-medical-workers\/embed\/#?secret=YTbQQyl72t#?secret=edXwIkzxvL\" data-secret=\"edXwIkzxvL\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup Doctolib has announced that is has raised a new funding round. \/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1460"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1460"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1460"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576885804,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/vertical-saas\/","name":"vertical SaaS","slug":"vertical-saas","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576885804"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576885804"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576885804"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2283992,"date":"2022-03-14T22:00:35","date_gmt":"2022-03-15T05:00:35","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2283992"},"modified":"2022-03-15T07:27:08","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T14:27:08","slug":"motto-to-launch-a-new-electric-bike-subscription-service-in-paris","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/motto-to-launch-a-new-electric-bike-subscription-service-in-paris\/","title":{"rendered":"Motto to launch a new electric bike subscription service in Paris"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Meet <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ridemotto.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Motto<\/a>, a new French startup that plans to offer electric bikes in Paris. Instead of buying those bikes, Motto customers will be able to rent them for a fixed price of \u20ac75 per month (around $82 at today\u2019s exchange rate).<\/p>\n<p>Customers get Motto-branded electric bikes with a motor in the rear wheel that helps you pedal up to a speed of 25km\/h. It has integrated lights, a GPS tracker and an anti-theft system. It features a carbon belt and the battery is removable.<\/p>\n<p>The battery is integrated into the seat tube, meaning that you can access the battery by removing the saddle and taking it with you. There are two different models, a step-over model and a low-step model. The frame is slightly different but everything else is identical.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283992\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>But Motto doesn\u2019t want to stop at hardware. Users aren\u2019t just renting a bike &#8212; they\u2019re subscribing to a service. The monthly subscription fee includes damage and theft insurance, as well as on-demand maintenance and repairs.<\/p>\n<p>When there\u2019s something wrong with your Motto bike, you can open the app and request a repair within 48 hours. In the near future, Motto plans to offer a baby carrier and a front rack as subscription add-ons.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283997\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283997\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2283997\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg 3986w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=300,187 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=768,480 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=680,425 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=2048,1279 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Motto-2.jpeg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283997\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Motto<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The startup has raised a $4.4 million (\u20ac4 million) seed round led by Cassius Family and Founders Future. Several business angels are also participating. Before rebranding to Motto, the startup was originally called Bloom, and 200 users tested the service in Paris already.<\/p>\n<p>And everybody will be able to sign up and get a bike starting in April 2022. The startup will compete with other bike subscription services, such as German startup <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/e-bike-subscription-service-dance-adds-new-cities-and-mopeds\/\">Dance<\/a>, Netherlands company <a href=\"https:\/\/swapfiets.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Swapfiets<\/a> and publicly funded service <a href=\"https:\/\/www.veligo-location.fr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">V\u00e9ligo<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>More importantly, the startup competes with public transportation, bike-sharing schemes and buying your own electric bike. The bike-as-a-service model provides many advantages.<\/p>\n<p>First, you don\u2019t have to pay a large sum of money upfront. Second, many bike owners don\u2019t want to get an electric bike because of thefts. Third, many people want to make sure they can actually use a bike to commute before buying one.<\/p>\n<p>For all these reasons, it\u2019s good to see that bike-as-a-service represents another interesting option to get started with bikes. I still believe that we\u2019re at the very start of the urban mobility revolution and people will end up using different transportation methods to get from point A to point B \u2014 especially in European cities. And many people should consider services like Motto to add an electric bike to their personal transportation mix.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZK9t0H3VXz\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/20\/how-four-european-cities-are-embracing-micromobility-to-drive-out-cars\/\">How four European cities are embracing micromobility to drive out cars<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;How four European cities are embracing micromobility to drive out cars&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/20\/how-four-european-cities-are-embracing-micromobility-to-drive-out-cars\/embed\/#?secret=LNIIT686qF#?secret=ZK9t0H3VXz\" data-secret=\"ZK9t0H3VXz\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Meet Motto, a new French startup that plans to offer electric bikes in Paris. Instead of buying those bikes, Motto customers will be able to rent them for a fixed price of \u20ac75 per month (around $82 at today\u2019s exchange rate). Customers get Motto-branded electric bikes with a motor in the rear wheel that helps thinks companies should rent laptops instead of buying them"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fleet.co\">Fleet<\/a> wants to become your IT department\u2019s best friend by managing hardware as a service. Fleet clients can rent computers and smartphones for a flat monthly fee. If there\u2019s a hardware issue, the startup handles returns and repairs.<\/p>\n<p>And when it\u2019s time to renew, Fleet can exchange old corporate laptops and smartphones for new ones. Customers can see their current fleet of devices in a single admin interface.<\/p>\n<p>The company offers a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fleet.co\/en\/location-ordinateurs\/tarifs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wide range of devices<\/a>. For instance, a 14-inch MacBook Pro with an M1 Pro chip and 16GB of RAM currently costs \u20ac99.90 per device per month. The M1 MacBook Air starts at \u20ac54.90 per device per month. An iPhone 13 with 128GB of storage will cost you \u20ac44.90 per month.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283465\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>You can also find Microsoft laptops (Surface Laptop Go, Surface Laptop 4 and Surface Pro 7), Dell computers and even a couple of Chromebooks. When a device is reaching its end of life and is sent back to Fleet, the company gives it to a nonprofit organization, sells it to a refurbishment company or recycles it.<\/p>\n<p>Fleet is a bootstrapped startup and hasn\u2019t raised any VC funding. But it\u2019s been growing nicely as the company is expected to generate an annual turnover of $13.1 million (\u20ac12 million) at its current run rate.<\/p>\n<p>It currently has 600 clients including some well-known French startups, such as Ankorstore, Ornikar, Sunday, Matera, Cubyn, Wemaintain and Shine. And today, the company is launching its device-as-a-service offering in Spain. The company is going to open an office in Barcelona as well.<\/p>\n<p>There are more European expansions on the road map as many of Fleet\u2019s suppliers can deliver across Europe already. The company is looking at Portugal, Italy, Germany and Belgium for its next markets.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Many companies choose to buy devices for their employees directly. But there\u2019s a big upfront cost and it means that you don\u2019t have any supplier that can help you in case of hardware issues.<\/p>\n<p>Companies have been looking at ways to turn these big capital expenditures into operating costs. For instance, a company could negotiate a credit line with their bank to buy hardware.<\/p>\n<p>And this is key to understanding Fleet\u2019s business model. The startup negotiates directly with financial partners and leasing companies so that Fleet clients just have to create an account and submit some documents. They can order some laptops in just a few minutes. Fleet then becomes another service provider that does the heavy lifting for you.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"N9Pb11cSFU\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/15\/why-startups-may-want-to-rent-hardware-instead-of-buying-it\/\">Why startups may want to rent hardware instead of buying it<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Why startups may want to rent hardware instead of buying it&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/15\/why-startups-may-want-to-rent-hardware-instead-of-buying-it\/embed\/#?secret=x78w6qzana#?secret=N9Pb11cSFU\" data-secret=\"N9Pb11cSFU\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>French startup Fleet wants to become your IT department\u2019s best friend by managing hardware as a service. Fleet clients can rent computers and smartphones for a flat monthly fee. If there\u2019s a hardware issue, the startup handles returns and repairs. And when it\u2019s time to renew, Fleet can exchange old corporate laptops and smartphones for [&hellip;]<\/p>\n","protected":false},"author":7636871,"featured_media":2283466,"comment_status":"open","ping_status":"closed","sticky":false,"template":"","format":"standard","meta":{"outcome":"","status":"","crunchbase_tag":0,"amp_status":"","relegenceEntities":[],"relegenceSubjects":[],"carmot_uuid":"2564ceda-4aea-37a6-936d-41b73bf39ed7"},"categories":[449557100,20429],"tags":[449551534,1169,508331,449557079,115000,1189346,38616],"crunchbase_tag":[],"tc_stories_tax":[],"tc_ec_category":[],"tc_event":[],"jetpack_featured_media_url":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/jeremy-bezanger-2jCNW_PSfFo-unsplash.jpg","parsely":{"version":"1.0.0","meta":{"@context":"http:\/\/schema.org","@type":"WebPage","headline":"Deepki
