surface","slug":"microsoft-surface","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/1189346"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=1189346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1189346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1189346"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1189346"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":38616,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/smartphones\/","name":"smartphones","slug":"smartphones","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/38616"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=38616"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=38616"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=38616"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=38616"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2276327,"date":"2022-03-09T00:00:19","date_gmt":"2022-03-09T08:00:19","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2276327"},"modified":"2022-03-09T09:53:08","modified_gmt":"2022-03-09T17:53:08","slug":"atlantic-money-wants-to-challenge-wise-with-even-cheaper-international-money-transfers","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/atlantic-money-wants-to-challenge-wise-with-even-cheaper-international-money-transfers\/","title":{"rendered":"Atlantic Money wants to challenge Wise with even cheaper international money transfers"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Meet <a href=\"https:\/\/atlantic.money\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Atlantic Money<\/a>, a foreign exchange startup that plans to be cheaper than other foreign exchange services. If that pitch sounds familiar, that\u2019s because <a href=\"https:\/\/wise.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wise<\/a>, the company formerly known as TransferWise, originally appeared on the startup scene with the same promise.<\/p>\n<p>And yet, Atlantic Money thinks that even Wise and Revolut are too expensive. According to the company, they try to do too many things at once and they end up charging customers for things they don\u2019t need.<\/p>\n<p>How much will you pay for international money transfers on Atlantic Money? The company will charge a \u00a33 flat fee and that\u2019s it. There will be no markup on the exchange rate that they can secure.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2276327\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>For small transfers, \u00a33 is quite a lot. But once you start transferring more than \u00a31,000, Atlantic Money becomes more competitive.<\/p>\n<p>And this is key to Atlantic Money\u2019s business model. Instead of charging progressive fees, the startup wants to move to a fixed, per transaction fee.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281216\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281216\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281216\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"684\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg 7992w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=768,513 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=1536,1026 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=2048,1367 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-2.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281216\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Atlantic Money<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Founded by Neeraj Baid and Patrick Kavanagh, the pair originally met in their previous jobs at <a href=\"https:\/\/robinhood.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Robinhood<\/a>. The startup has raised a $4.5 million seed round led by <a href=\"http:\/\/amplovc.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amplo<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/ribbitcap.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ribbit Capital<\/a>. Robinhood\u2019s founders Vlad Tenev and Baiju Bhatt also invested in the company. Webull\u2019s Anquan Wang is an investor as well.<\/p>\n<p>The startup is launching a handful of corridors at first. More specifically, users who sign up today can send money from the U.K. in GBP into nine currencies \u2014 USD, EUR, AUD, CAD, SEK, NOK, DKK, PLN and CZK. When it comes to payment methods, Atlantic Money currently focuses on local bank transfers. Standard transfers take two to three business days while express transfers should arrive within a day.<\/p>\n<p>Behind the scenes, the company partners with several large financial institutions that can provide a good foreign exchange rate. Atlantic Money picks the best rate and doesn\u2019t add any markup fee. It\u2019s going to be interesting to see if Atlantic Money can provide better rates than its competitors.<\/p>\n<p>At the time of writing, when you try to transfer \u00a35,000 to the U.S., it currently costs \u00a317.79 in fees on Wise \u2014 you receive $6,648.51. With a free Revolut account, you pay \u00a320.96 in fees in addition to the \u00a35,000 you want to convert. However, the exchange rate is slightly better as you receive around $6,700 in exchange for \u00a35,020.96.<\/p>\n<p>Of course, Revolut provides other services, such as bank accounts, cards, the ability to trade stocks and cryptocurrencies, etc. You can pay \u00a36.99 per month for a premium account and waive fees on currency exchange. However, it\u2019s a 12-month plan, so you may end up paying more in subscription fees than in FX fees depending on your Revolut usage.<\/p>\n<p>Similarly, Wise lets you generate local account details in a dozen countries, which could be useful to get paid in a country where you don\u2019t live. Wise also tries to make transfers as quick as possible \u2014 45% of Wise transfers <a href=\"https:\/\/wise.com\/gb\/blog\/mission-update-q4-2021-speed\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">arrive<\/a> in 20 seconds or less.<\/p>\n<p>In other words, there is room for more than just one foreign exchange product. It\u2019s not a one-size-fits-all industry. Customers will end up picking a service depending on the corridor they use most often, their average transfer size and the additional features they might need. But if you just want to move large amounts from the U.K. to Europe or Northern America, you could potentially become an Atlantic Money user.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281215\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281215\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281215\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"613\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg 1270w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg?resize=150,90 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg?resize=300,180 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg?resize=768,460 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg?resize=680,407 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Atlantic-Money-1.jpeg?resize=50,30 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281215\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Atlantic Money<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Meet Atlantic Money, a foreign exchange startup that plans to be cheaper than other foreign exchange services. If that pitch sounds familiar, that\u2019s because Wise, the company formerly known as TransferWise, originally appeared on the startup scene with the same promise. And yet, Atlantic Money thinks that even Wise and Revolut are too expensive. He was the first person to cover N26, Revolut and DigitalOcean. He has written scoops on large acquisitions from Apple, Microsoft and Snap.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>When he\u2019s not writing, Romain is also a developer \u2014 he understands how the tech behind the tech works. He also has a deep historical knowledge of the computer industry for the past 50 years. He knows how to connect the dots between innovations and the effect on the fabric of our society.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Romain graduated from Emlyon Business School, a leading French business school specialized in entrepreneurship. He has helped several non-profit organizations, such as StartHer, an organization that promotes education and empowerment of women in technology, and Techfugees, an organization that empowers displaced people with technology.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Disclosure: Romain owns small amounts of various Capital","slug":"ribbit-capital","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/117949477"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=117949477"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=117949477"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=117949477"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=117949477"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281459,"date":"2022-03-08T23:00:41","date_gmt":"2022-03-09T07:00:41","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281459"},"modified":"2022-03-09T06:53:58","modified_gmt":"2022-03-09T14:53:58","slug":"e-bike-subscription-service-dance-adds-new-cities-and-mopeds","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/e-bike-subscription-service-dance-adds-new-cities-and-mopeds\/","title":{"rendered":"E-bike subscription service Dance adds new cities and mopeds"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">After raising <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/27\/dance-raises-another-19-4-million-for-its-e-bike-subscription-service\/\">nearly $20 million<\/a> a few months ago, Berlin-based startup <a href=\"https:\/\/dance.co\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dance<\/a> is expanding its electric bike subscription service to a handful of new cities. In addition to Berlin, people living in Hamburg, Munich, Vienna and Paris will be able to rent an e-bike for a fixed monthly price.<\/p>\n<p>Dance isn\u2019t just another e-bike manufacturer; the company designed e-bikes specifically to rent to customers. The Dance One has integrated lights, a carbon belt, hydraulic discs and a smartphone mount on the handlebar. You can unlock the battery to charge it at home without having to bring your bike inside.<\/p>\n<p>Customers can reserve their own Dance bike for \u20ac79 per month, which includes both theft protection and repairs. When there\u2019s something wrong with your bike, you can schedule a repair over the next 24 hours. That\u2019s part of the reason why Dance is limited to a handful of cities.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281459\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The startup doesn\u2019t plan to stop at e-bikes, though. The company\u2019s goal is to accelerate urban mobility changes with a complete offering. That\u2019s why Dance has quietly acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/rollich.de\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rollich<\/a>, an electric moped leasing company based in Berlin. Terms of the acquisition remain undisclosed, though Rollich founder Felix Schaar is joining Dance.<\/p>\n<p>Essentially, Dance wants to focus on moving people across cities. Lighter vehicles, such as electric mopeds and bikes, combined with services should help when it comes to congestion and urban pollution.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOur goal at Dance has always been to spark a global movement towards creating safer, more livable cities by offering a flexible and convenient way to travel,\u201d co-founder and CEO Eric Quidenus-Wahlforss said in a statement. \u201cNow is the right time: with increased cycling infrastructure, public discourse and political will across Europe to create more sustainable cities, we can help more people choose a more sustainable commute.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281463\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281463\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281463\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png 3840w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Moped_Perspective.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281463\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Dance<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Dance is partnering with NIU for its mopeds. It sounds like Dance is mostly rebranding existing NIU mopeds and integrating them with its service. Mopeds will only be available in Germany for now.<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s another new vehicle in the lineup, as you can see in the photo at the top of the article, which looks like an ad for car-free cities with a car-ad budget. Dance is introducing a low-step variant of its electric bike. It works pretty much like its existing e-bike, but with a different frame that&#8217;s more suitable for shorter people.<\/p>\n<p>While Dance originally focused on no-commitment plans, customers can now choose to pay for a yearly subscription and get a small rebate.<\/p>\n<p>E-bikes now cost \u20ac79 per month, or \u20ac59 per month if you\u2019re willing to pay for a yearly subscription. Mopeds cost \u20ac119 per month, or \u20ac89 per month with a 12-month plan. Right now, plans are a bit cheaper due to introductory prices.<\/p>\n<p>Finally, Dance wants to address the B2B market with a new Dance for Business offering. This service isn\u2019t designed for quick-commerce or food delivery companies. Instead, companies can leverage Dance for Business to offer the option to get an e-bike as an employee benefit.<\/p>\n<p>This is a smart move as many companies already pay for public transportation passes. The ability to choose between a public transportation pass and an e-bike would be nice for many employees.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281461\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281461\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281461\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png 3840w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/dance_Lowstep_Side0.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281461\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Dance<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>After raising nearly $20 million a few months ago, Berlin-based startup Dance is expanding its electric bike subscription service to a handful of new cities. In addition to Berlin, people living in Hamburg, Munich, Vienna and Paris will be able to rent an e-bike for a fixed monthly price. Dance isn\u2019t just another e-bike manufacturer;
